  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_38e43217-cafb-47eb-8010-3b0ea7799ecf'
      });
    }

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book is to "die" for! (Get it?) Anyway, this book is basically filled the case of mistaken identity, full-blown humor, and irony that screams so <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book is to "die" for! (Get it?) Anyway, this book is basically filled the case of mistaken identity, full-blown humor, and irony that screams so loud, I'm surprised I haven't lost my hearing. You should never question a book. Just pick it up and see if it's your thing. I would definitely recommend you read it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

For more info on this challenge, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/16216645-urr-s-new-years-2018-romance-reading-challenge' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here</a>. 💙   <br/><br/><br/><br/>It's been so long since I read a "bad" book that I had almost forgotten what the experience was like! Thank goodness BOYS THAT BITE came to remind me, lest I grow soft and foolhardy in my ignorance.<br/><br/><br/><br/>BOYS THAT BITE is about two sisters named...Sunny and Rayne. Sunny is </span>
  <span id="freeText2073825223735372543" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>💙 I read this for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers" rel="nofollow noopener">Unapologetic Romance Readers</a>' <b>New Years 2018 Reading Challenge</b>, for the category of: <i>Vampire Romance</i>. For more info on this challenge, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/16216645-urr-s-new-years-2018-romance-reading-challenge" rel="nofollow noopener">click here</a>. 💙   <br><br><br><br>It's been so long since I read a "bad" book that I had almost forgotten what the experience was like! Thank goodness BOYS THAT BITE came to remind me, lest I grow soft and foolhardy in my ignorance.<br><br><br><br>BOYS THAT BITE is about two sisters named...Sunny and Rayne. Sunny is a prep and Rayne is a goth. (This book was written in 2006, when such distinctions were important.) One day, Rayne drags Sunny to a Goth club and Sunny accidentally gets bitten by a vampire named Magnus. It turns out that he was actually supposed to bite <i>Rayne</i>, who has spent years on a special waiting list for the privilege, but because they're twins...oops!<br><br><br><br>The next two hundred something pages consists of plot devices that can be summed up with statements that start with "OMG" and end with exclamation points:<br><br><br><br>OMG, now I'm totally going to be a vampire and that sucks because I'll miss prom!<br><br><br><br>OMG, but the vampire that bit me is kind of hot, though!<br><br><br><br>OMG, now there's a vampire slayer but she's totes fat you guys, ew yuck! But also LOL!<br><br><br><br>OMG, but what about that sexy jock that I like! OMG, being a vampire means excreting pheromones that make EVERYONE like me, including dirty old man teachers, ew yuck!<br><br><br><br>OMG, so it turns out that maybe I can become a human again if I drink from the Holy Grail!<br><br><br><br>OMG, but that hot vampire though!<br><br><br><br>OMG, flying on a private jet to England!<br><br><br><br>OMG, prom with my sexy jock boyfriend!<br><br><br><br>OMG, that hot vampire guy though!<br><br><br><br>OMG, my twin sister is a selfish meanie and I hate her so much!<br><br><br><br>OMG, I'm a vampire!<br><br><br><br>This is one of those books that was clearly written with the idea that teenagers are vapid creatures who see all other girls as rivals to be jealous of (Rayne), slut-shame (Rayne), or fat-shame (the vampire slayer). Sunny was intolerable as a narrator, and a useless trash person as a human being. It's been a while since I read a character who was so selfish and shallow who I wasn't supposed to hate. The attempts to inject pop-culture and teen-speak into this book also feel really embarrassing and dated. I grabbed this book when it was free for Kindle a few months ago and I kind of wonder if it was rewritten to be more "modern" and "hip"? Because this book was written in 2006, mind, and yet, the book mentions Taylor Swift (and calls her "T-Swizzle"), the Kardashians are mentioned, and at one point, Sunny says she looks like "Jennifer Laurence." None of those things were hugely relevant in 2006. Those are more like 2016 pop culture references. On the other hand, the references and pervasiveness of Goth culture and punk culture and bands like Green Day make this book feel way more like an early 2000s effort. If this book was edited to be more "modern," it failed miserably, because now it comes across as this Frankenstein effort written by an alien who only understands teenagers from what they have seen on reruns of after school specials.<br><br><br><br>I'm really annoyed because I wanted to like this book. I love vampire stories, and I even love teenage vampire stories like TWILIGHT. This book wanted to be TWILIGHT but it also wanted to be edgy, and ended up sacrificing the love story that made TWILIGHT so epic for annoying teenage drama and ended up sacrificing the edginess for "OMG, I'm so relatable you guys! G to the whizzle! I'm hip and I'm straight-edge and I'm here to shake the scene, tubular-style!"-type shenanigans that kind of made me feel like I was watching a friend's dad try to sound cool at a barbecue. Oh, and that insta-love. That <i>insta-love</i>. It made TWILIGHT look like <i>A Very Long Engagement</i>.<br><br><br><br>I think I'll be giving the rest of this author's books a miss.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>
  <a data-text-id="2073825223735372543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText14624858419561058975" style="display:none">I didn't get far into this book.. just far enough.<br /><br />I believe the lead characters are 16 years of age? There abouts. This book reads like it was written by a 16 year old. <br /><br />OMG!! Nooooo wayyyyy!!<br />Yesssssss wayyyyyy! <div id="review_152805991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152805991" />
    <a title="Patricia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5035742-patricia"><img alt="Patricia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344007670p2/5035742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152805991?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia" href="/user/show/5035742-patricia">Patricia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">nobody?</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5035742-patricia?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5035742-patricia?shelf=r_old-review">r_old-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5035742-patricia?shelf=review-on-old-blog">review-on-old-blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152805991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1187723692123943165">It’s been some time since I’ve read this. I orig­i­nally reviewed it in Ger­man, but decided to trans­late it into Eng­lish. (I’m redesign­ing my blog) So, if I got some things wrong, please humor me.<br/><br/>I have no idea where to start. It started with that moment where I sat in front of my bookshelves and thought I'd need something new and special and fresh, and yes, my tbr-pile has started talking to me at this point, but what wouldn't I give for something amazing. Instead, I got Boys That Bite. A b</span>
  <span id="freeText1187723692123943165" style="display:none">It’s been some time since I’ve read this. I orig­i­nally reviewed it in Ger­man, but decided to trans­late it into Eng­lish. (I’m redesign­ing my blog) So, if I got some things wrong, please humor me.<br /><br />I have no idea where to start. It started with that moment where I sat in front of my bookshelves and thought I'd need something new and special and fresh, and yes, my tbr-pile has started talking to me at this point, but what wouldn't I give for something amazing. Instead, I got Boys That Bite. A book so awful that it had me crawl out of bed despite being sick, just to talk about how little I enjoyed it. <br /><br />I'm possibly being really harsh, but still. Boys that Bite was quite horrible.<br /><br />First of all — There are no boys. The guys are old. Ancient. Vam­pires. So, the title is mis­lead­ing, but that’d be okay if the con­tent was suf­fer­able. <br /><br />But it wasn't. I'm not sure what urged the author to create characters with so little dimension that readers'd fear imploding books, but there you have it. I was so close to DNFing this novel, I might as well just have.<br /><br />There are two roads I could go here: Either I'll complain about the injustice done to Sunnie (the main character, without personality except for that of a whiney, melodramatic toad) or about the fact that Magnus, a thousand year old vampire, would actually go for children. Had he just bitchslapped the hell out of this entire book, I'd have been slightly less judgemental.<br /><br />Okay, the best thing would have been for Sunny to wake up and suddenly realise that she was an actual human being, with the complexity of one, but let's just not.<br /><br />Sun­shine has Hipster-parents and a twin-sister named Rayne, who except for being her twin and shar­ing her DNA has noth­ing in com­mon with her. She’s also a Goth. Or something resembling that, I suppose. No joking.<br /><br />While Sunnie’s is des­per­ately hop­ing for Jake Wilder, one of the pop­u­lar guys, to ask her to prom, Rayne wants to become a vam­pire. She then takes Sun­nie to a disco, where she should’ve been made. Except that the guy who should trans­form her mis­takes Sun­nie for her and infects her with the vampire-virus.<br /><br />Des­per­ate, Sun­nie tries to fight the virus and stay human, but along the 7 days-journey she falls in love with Mag­nus. Who is 10xHugh Heffner.<br /><br />I’d like to point out what I liked about the book, but there is almost to com­pletely noth­ing. It was a quick read, thank God, some­times almost nice. Those times are the scenes with­out Sun­nie or Magnus.. or any of the characters.. Oh wait.<br /><br />Her imma­ture (I hate that word, actu­ally) atti­tude destroys any appeal this novel could have had, though. Plus, this seems to be the one book that didn’t hes­i­tate to use every stereo­type out there and some. Edwa– I mean, Mag­nus, who is a mil­lenia old and should log­i­cally be very wise gets involved with a teenager? Sri­ously? And why is Rayne tak­ing her sis­ter with her to the disco/club? Not only are the characters walking staples, the plot downright ridiculous, it didn't seem self-aware. You can kinda enjoy books that are intentionally bad.<br /><br />How is it pos­si­ble to fall in love with a man, whom you don’t know at all? Why would some­one make the deci­sions this hero­ine did? Why the ones the hero did? Because there <i>are</i> books where someone falls instantly in love and you buy that, right? Just.. not this one.<br /><br />It can’t be okay to propagate a book like this, were the reader is actu­ally told that in order to be happy you need a boyfriend and that as long as the guy looks like he’s 18 years old it doesn’t mat­ter that he’s older than Hugh Heffner.<br /><br />There is this extreme dif­fer­ence between the mind of a 15 and a 18 years old per­son. Three years of life expe­ri­ences make a huge dif­fer­ence. What do 985 years do to a per­son? (I won’t even start with the mat­ing bond-shit..)<br /><br /><b>Bot­tom line:</b><br /><br />For edu­ca­tional pur­poses it should be for­bid­den for peo­ple below the age of 16 to read this book. That much self­ishnes, self­pity and stu­pid­ity in a per­son who is the pro­tag­o­nist, for God’s sake, is unbearable, especially when the narration and worldbuilding just work it as if it's normal.<br /><br />And if you have a hint of moral val­ues you wouldn’t allow any­one over the age of 15 to read the book, because as sorry as I am, it was tor­ture to spend 2 hours with those folks. I’d rather have taken a shower. Tidied up my room. Talked to my 90 years old neighbour.. (I don't have that neighbour. I'd talk to my 90 year old imaginary neighbour.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1187723692123943165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218672535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2998059895580611225">Boys That Bite sounds interesting. The synopsis is enough that you think you're going to get a pretty good book.<br/>I, personally, found this to be the suckiest vampire book (pun<br/>intended). <br/><br/>I was the victim of falling for a pretty cover and in the course of falling, my brain was turned to mush. No, really, I'm not kidding.<br/><br/>Sunny is the most annoying character in the history of annoying characters. She's interested in Jake Wilder, the guy who's super popular, with bedroom eyes- of course, he has no ide</span>
  <span id="freeText2998059895580611225" style="display:none">Boys That Bite sounds interesting. The synopsis is enough that you think you're going to get a pretty good book.<br />I, personally, found this to be the suckiest vampire book (pun<br />intended). <br /><br />I was the victim of falling for a pretty cover and in the course of falling, my brain was turned to mush. No, really, I'm not kidding.<br /><br />Sunny is the most annoying character in the history of annoying characters. She's interested in Jake Wilder, the guy who's super popular, with bedroom eyes- of course, he has no idea she exists.<br />Enter Magnus. Vampire. Major hottie. British. Sapphire eyes. Once a knight of King Arthur's. A thousand years old. She falls for him at once. Magnus, mistakenly bites Sunny thinking that she is her twin sister Rayne. Yes, Rayne. Sunshine and Rayne. Rayne is described as a typical 'goth' kid. Black clothes. Long black skirts. Black makeup. Extraordinarily pale. Rayne was supposed to have been turned into a vampire the night Sunny was bit. Heck, she even had her certificate in training on how to be vampire. Not to mention she runs a blog that is mentioned every five seconds<br /><br />Now, the book wasn't too bad, but once you get past chapter 6, it just...sucks. Every character is compared to their celebrity counter-part. Orlando Blood (Pirates of the Caribbean Orlando, not Lord of the Rings Orlando). Brad Pitt. Haley Joel Osment. I couldn't read a page without there being some kind of comparison to something 'famous'.<br /><br />Boys that Bite also takes an ode from Buffy...There are slayers, "Once a generation a girl is born who is destined to slay the vampire."<br />Sound familiar?<br /> <br />The way the book is written feels more like it's geared to people who are 15 or less. I didn't connect with any of the characters and I didn't enjoy the writing. The whole time I wished for the ride to be over. And it's one ride I won't ever get on again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2998059895580611225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2109887218" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15836437349289088882"><b>This book is so bad!</b><br/>Not only is it full of Vampire clichés, it's also really terrible written.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506385513ra/24011167.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, ok... let me calm down a bit....<br/>First let me start off with saying that I had this book on my shelf for forever.<br/>I knew that it would be bad and full of clichés, but I still picked it up because my challange for this month was to read a book that has been forever on my shelves, so here I am. Reading it. Finishing it. Writting a review for it.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506385513ra/24011168.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Sunny and her twin Rayne could be no more different</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15836437349289088882" style="display:none"><b>This book is so bad!</b><br>Not only is it full of Vampire clichés, it's also really terrible written.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506385513ra/24011167.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, ok... let me calm down a bit....<br>First let me start off with saying that I had this book on my shelf for forever.<br>I knew that it would be bad and full of clichés, but I still picked it up because my challange for this month was to read a book that has been forever on my shelves, so here I am. Reading it. Finishing it. Writting a review for it.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506385513ra/24011168.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Sunny and her twin Rayne could be no more different even if they didn't look alike. <br>(You see, their mother somehow knew what kind of personalities her daughters would have and named them accordingly.)<br>While Sunny is your normal teenage student that has a crush on the most popular guy in school, (even tho she is sure that he doesn't know she excist), Rayn on the other hand isn't.<br>She is more of your typical goth girl who owns only black clothes and is into dark stuff like Vampires. So much she even wants to become on of them and actually manages to close a deal with them to make her one.<br>Only when she and her sister go out in a club, the said Vampire mistakes them and bites Sunny instead of Rayne.<br>Even tho Sunny doesn't belive them at the beginning, she starts to panic and wants a way out of this. She doesn't want to become a Vampire, so she and the Vampire Magnus, are on the hunt for the antidote that will make her human again.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br>The Vampire-Romance clichés didn't bother me as much as the narrator did.<br><b>Sunny is the most annoying narrator I've ever read from!</b><br>It's written in first POV and it drove me crazy.<br><b>It is so full of 00's pop culture that it actually pained me to read this book even tho it was short and fast paced.</b> We literally didn't get any single sentence that didn't was accompanied by some pop culture refrence.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><i><b><u>Actual Quotes from the Book:</u></b><br>•I gasp as my eyes become accustomed to the dim light and I see what we've walked into. It's like a mansion. An un-derground mansion. With cathedral ceilings, floors made of marble, and the most elegant furnishings I've ever seen. I can see why they need Fort Knox-like security down here. It's a tomb raider's dream come true. Lara Croft would have a field day.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>•At the end of the hall, we enter a lobby where a thin, blond woman sits behind a desk, filing her nails and looking bored. She looks like someone I know, but I can't seem to place her.<br><br>"Hi, Marcia," Magnus says, addressing her politely.<br><br>That's it! She looks like Marcia Brady from the The Brady Bunch. Heh.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>• Lucifent's office turns out to be as deluxe as the rest of the underground coven. The only thing missing is windows. I'd hate the no-windows thing, were I to become a permanent vamp. Though the Picassos on the wall might make up for their absence somewhat. The floors are made of gleaming hardwood and a giant mahogany desk lies in the center of the room.<br><br>Behind the desk sits Haley Joel Osment, the little kid from that creepy Sixth Sense movie.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>• Suddenly, milliseconds before he can spit out the knowl-edge that will save me from eternal damnation, warning sirens start going off. They sound like something you'd hear on a Star Trek episode, moments before the Enterprise self-destructs. Or after Homer Simpson does something stupid yet again at the Springfield nuclear power plant.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>• She's dressed in black leather, but don't get the mistaken impression that she's at all attractive and sexy in it. Let's just say Bertha the Vampire Slayer has evidently been hitting the drive-through a few too many times on her dinner break. And leather sure isn't very forgiving when it comes to super sizing your French fries. Especially tight, low-rise leather pants that allow her stomach fat to ooze out her front. Add a greasy zit-face and the stringy blond hair and you'll get a good mental picture of what this "Slayer" looks like.<br><br>I think I prefer Sarah Michelle Gellar.<br><br>"Lucifent," she snarls, raising her wooden stake. Wow, she's got braces too. I can't believe the mortal enemy of all vampires goes to an orthodontist. "Prepare to die."</i><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>And so many more. The book is full of them.<br>So yeah, it's safe to say that I won't be continuing on with this series even tho I would have if the narriation didn't make me want to rip my hair out.<br><br>If you want to give it a shot, be my guest but don't say that I didn't warn you.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454552515ra/17980545.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1420355-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240526410p2/1420355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111704402?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/1420355-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1420355-tina?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111704402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18368317159380557629">This is not my cup of tea. The writing is too juvenile for me to be interested. The protagonist is bitten and will soon transform into a full fledge vampire. How does she act ... silly, non-chalant, cracking jokes and just being lame. It's completely non-realistic. The cover is misleading. It's pretty and on the serious side. I thought I was getting a deep well thought out story line. Far from it. <br/><br/>This was silly, and not in a fun way. The author tried to hard to be funny. It ended up sounding li</span>
  <span id="freeText18368317159380557629" style="display:none">This is not my cup of tea. The writing is too juvenile for me to be interested. The protagonist is bitten and will soon transform into a full fledge vampire. How does she act ... silly, non-chalant, cracking jokes and just being lame. It's completely non-realistic. The cover is misleading. It's pretty and on the serious side. I thought I was getting a deep well thought out story line. Far from it. <br /><br />This was silly, and not in a fun way. The author tried to hard to be funny. It ended up sounding like a vampire spoof that wasn't meant to be a spoof. I enjoy YA but this is more pre-teen silly style. <br /><br /><br />Things that left me saying "What?" ( and this is all at the beginning of the book!) ...<br /><br />* The vampire coven secretary is named Marcia and looks like Marcia Brady.<br />* The coven's leader is a young kid that looks like Haley Joel Osmond!<br />* Sunshine talks to the coven leader like a little kid saying stupid things to him - ex. "Hey, you." " You're so cute." She's just annoying and her actions are fake.<br />* Vampire slayer is Bertha. Who is described as over weight, greasy zit-face, stringy blond hair slayer. "She wears tight, low-rise leather pants that allow her stomach fat to ooze out her front".<br />* Berths slays the all powerful and might coven leader in about 2 seconds. The lamest fight scene ever written. <br /><br />Overall it was to silly for my taste. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18368317159380557629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25265097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25265097" />
    <a title="Jai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20432-jai"><img alt="Jai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332689190p2/20432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17353979617531933391">Sunshine is the innocent and sweet identical twin to her dark goth sister Rayne, and one night when Rayne takes her to goth hangout Club Fang, Sunny is mistaken for Rayne. Unfortunately for her, its vampire Magnus, who was assigned to Rayne as her bloodmate that makes the mistake and he bites her and turns her into a vampire. What follows is the story of Sunshine trying to become human again while also insisting she be able to go to the prom. She also insists she does not like Magnus, even thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText17353979617531933391" style="display:none">Sunshine is the innocent and sweet identical twin to her dark goth sister Rayne, and one night when Rayne takes her to goth hangout Club Fang, Sunny is mistaken for Rayne. Unfortunately for her, its vampire Magnus, who was assigned to Rayne as her bloodmate that makes the mistake and he bites her and turns her into a vampire. What follows is the story of Sunshine trying to become human again while also insisting she be able to go to the prom. She also insists she does not like Magnus, even though bloodmates are supposed to be connected forever after a bite so you know where that's going. This was an easy, fast read, with some interesting worldbuilding (a chubby acned slayer, three month training, testing and a waiting list to get a vampire mate), but the characters were very one dimensional. I think this is the third/fourth time this month I've read a YA vamp novel featuring a goth character (Rayne) or a cheerleader type character (Sunny), and an older vampire in a young man's body who for some strange reason I can't fathom overlooks the foibles of teens and acts like a teen himself (Magnus). </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732159-keysha?shelf=in-my-bookshelf">in-my-bookshelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119782977" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2473077941123002911">If you expect a book type Twilight or Evernight I recommend you don’t read this book. Even if it posses all the elements of the books that I mention above the one thing that BTB doesn’t possess isthe element of love as Bella & Edward or Bianca & Lucas unconditional and irrevocably love I think that Mancusi main job of was to write a fun book, with a whole bunch of hilarious characters, with the vampires legends and folklore and of course a fun and light romance.<br/><br/>The main character, Sunshine aka S</span>
  <span id="freeText2473077941123002911" style="display:none">If you expect a book type Twilight or Evernight I recommend you don’t read this book. Even if it posses all the elements of the books that I mention above the one thing that BTB doesn’t possess isthe element of love as Bella &amp; Edward or Bianca &amp; Lucas unconditional and irrevocably love I think that Mancusi main job of was to write a fun book, with a whole bunch of hilarious characters, with the vampires legends and folklore and of course a fun and light romance.<br /><br />The main character, Sunshine aka Sunny, is the typical teenage adolescent who one day is worried about the dress she is going to wear to prom and the next day and without her consentment she has to deal with the fact that she’s a turning into a vampire and that she may stay that way forever if she doesn’t act fast. Mancusi doesn’t try to show us a very complex character just a normal girl thrown in a crazy situation, I even like her more than Elena from Vampire Diaries (Don’t flame me but I still and I don’t think I would ever like Elena). Of course there’s also the vampire, Magnus, who turn Sunny because he mistake her for her twin sister. He’s charming, funny, sexy and very sweet. He knows because of his mistake he has to do his best to help Sunny and well along the way he realize that maybe the shallow but sweet and very hard headed Sunny may be the one he’s destined to be with, but how so if she doesn’t want to be a vampire. See, who said that this book didn’t have any complication? <br />And of course the best thing about Magnus is that Mancusi describe him as he’s alike Orlando Bloom and that totally made my reading even more pleasant.<br /><br />At the end of the book there’s a big cliffhanger since we all now that Rayve story must be told and Mancusi may surprise you with what would be her new role in Stake That<br /><br />So if you want to read book with fun dialog, hilarious situation and breezy characters I think this would be fine choice for you. I think that this book accomplish what it was written for, for you to have a good time</span>

<div id="review_160275149" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160275149" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5153099-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467330927p2/5153099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160275149?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/5153099-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160275149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3651234465743701001"><br/>When I first read the synopsis of the book, I though it was cool, so I immediately tried it.<br/>Was I ever so wrong.<br/><br/>At first it <i>was</i> kind of good, or at least decent. <br/>Mari Mancusi introduced us to one of the twin sisters' life, Sunshine's.<br/>She's the average teenage girl, in love with the hot kid of high school, and trying to be someone.<br/>But soon she gets caught up in the vampire world, a world she's too reluctant to accept and understand.<br/><br/>This I did like.<br/>It's not like other chicks in book; when they're </span>
  <span id="freeText3651234465743701001" style="display:none"><br />When I first read the synopsis of the book, I though it was cool, so I immediately tried it.<br />Was I ever so wrong.<br /><br />At first it <i>was</i> kind of good, or at least decent. <br />Mari Mancusi introduced us to one of the twin sisters' life, Sunshine's.<br />She's the average teenage girl, in love with the hot kid of high school, and trying to be someone.<br />But soon she gets caught up in the vampire world, a world she's too reluctant to accept and understand.<br /><br />This I did like.<br />It's not like other chicks in book; when they're told who they're talking to is a vampire, and they're like "Whoa, really, I'm scared now."<br />No. <br />She laughs and thinks it's a joke, because REALLY, THAT'S what girls in books <i>should</i> do. This was a point in favor for Mari Mancusi.<br />But then the book starts to fall.<br />This "mission" they have to accomplish, the journey, the save-the-girl-and-come-back-home project. It was all SO badly written.<br />Seriously, this became one of the WORST book I've ever read.<br /><br />The ending was totally rushed out.<br />Apart from the fact that their "mission" was a total flop.<br />Like, they arrived to England, encountered basically no obstacle, went right into the right place and got the Holy Graal like it was all so simple. Yeah right.<br />Plus, at the end, one minute the girl was still *spoiler* a vampire, and the next she was human again, and you were left like "what happened". .__.<br /><br />I'm not going to lie, I've read the other books in the series, but that only for mere curiosity.<br />The storyline wasn't bad, so I was somehow hoping it would get better in the other books.<br />But every minute I read it became more and more ridiculous, really.<br />I am sorry Mari Mancusi, but this series is a total flop.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3651234465743701001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8398060989690324546">Synopsis: Due to the worst case of mistaken identity in the case of humanity, Magnus, a vampire hottie, went for Sunshine's innocent neck insted of her dark side loving twin sister Rayne who went thru the vampire testing to find her vampire mate, signed a contract to become a vampire, and even has her own vampire web site logging her journey into becoming a vampire.<br/><br/>Now if she doesn't reverse the bite in time, Magnus will be her blood mate forever and she's doomed to be a blood-gulping, pasty, da</span>
  <span id="freeText8398060989690324546" style="display:none">Synopsis: Due to the worst case of mistaken identity in the case of humanity, Magnus, a vampire hottie, went for Sunshine's innocent neck insted of her dark side loving twin sister Rayne who went thru the vampire testing to find her vampire mate, signed a contract to become a vampire, and even has her own vampire web site logging her journey into becoming a vampire.<br /><br />Now if she doesn't reverse the bite in time, Magnus will be her blood mate forever and she's doomed to be a blood-gulping, pasty, daylight-hating vampire. That would seriously bite; espcially after hotty Jake Wilder just asked her to the prom. <br /><br />Of course, things get loopy from here. With the unfortunate slaying of the vampire leader Lord Lucifant by Betsy the Vampire Slayer (seriously!) with a weight problem; Sunshine, Rayne, and Magnus must find the one thing that can solve her problem: the Holy Grail.<br /><br />They wish it were a joke but it's not. Magnus is also the newly crowned king of the coven, thanks to Lucifants untimely death. The ending is quite funny actually with Sunshine getting the surprise of her young life.<br /><br />This is the first book in the series and is mostly from Sunny's POV. Sunny and Rayne's mother is most definitely a flower child with her tofu loving recipes...yuck! This is a definite YA novel and geared towards those in HS.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9925332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12680518424079601423">All Sunny McDonald wants is to get through high school, get good grades, and get Sex God Jake Wilder to notice her. But when she reluctantly accompanies her identical twin sister Rayne to a Goth nightclub, Sunny gets more than she bargained for. Because Rayne has been studying to become a vampire, and her vampire mentor just bit Sunny instead. Now, Sunny’s on her way to eternal life. Fortunately, there’s a cure, if she can get to it in time. Unfortunately, the cure is the Holy Grail. Yes, the on</span>
  <span id="freeText12680518424079601423" style="display:none">All Sunny McDonald wants is to get through high school, get good grades, and get Sex God Jake Wilder to notice her. But when she reluctantly accompanies her identical twin sister Rayne to a Goth nightclub, Sunny gets more than she bargained for. Because Rayne has been studying to become a vampire, and her vampire mentor just bit Sunny instead. Now, Sunny’s on her way to eternal life. Fortunately, there’s a cure, if she can get to it in time. Unfortunately, the cure is the Holy Grail. Yes, the one and only. Now, Sunny, Rayne, and vampire hottie Magnus are on a race against time to turn Sunny back before she turns vampire forever.<br /><br />This book is extremely teen bubblegum. It’s fun and irreverent and silly, and a really good fast read, but that’s all it is. The plot twists are weak, the characters are shallow. The love story feels forced, and everything else feels like a vehicle for the love story. And Sunny really isn’t an engaging character of any sort.<br /><br />The ending opens the door for a more interesting looking sequel—or rather, a sequel that could either be more interesting, or a total Buffy knockoff.<br /></span>

<div id="review_234542109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234542109" />
    <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books"><img alt="Kayleigh {K-Books}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540157695p2/3996633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234542109?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh {K-Books}" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books">Kayleigh {K-Books}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3996633-kayleigh-k-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3996633-kayleigh-k-books?shelf=abandoned-series">abandoned-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234542109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5634630137461355171"><a href='http://k-booksxo.blogspot.com/2011/11/boys-that-bite-blood-coven-1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boys That Bite Review on K-Books</a><br/><br/>I didn't really know what to expect when I first started reading this book. After finishing it all I can say is: Why didn't I hear about this book sooner? I honestly can't believe that it was published 5 years ago. I really liked this book. It's such a light, funny read.<br/><br/>Sunny loves being human. She is a straight A student who never does anything wrong. She can't wait to graduate high school and start college. One thing could make her life better. Jake Wilder, most</span>
  <span id="freeText5634630137461355171" style="display:none"><a href="http://k-booksxo.blogspot.com/2011/11/boys-that-bite-blood-coven-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Boys That Bite Review on K-Books</a><br /><br />I didn't really know what to expect when I first started reading this book. After finishing it all I can say is: Why didn't I hear about this book sooner? I honestly can't believe that it was published 5 years ago. I really liked this book. It's such a light, funny read.<br /><br />Sunny loves being human. She is a straight A student who never does anything wrong. She can't wait to graduate high school and start college. One thing could make her life better. Jake Wilder, most popular guy in school and sex God could notice her. One thing she doesn't count on is finding out that vampires exist in the worse possible way. Being mistaken for her Goth-Vampire-Loving twin sister Rayne, Sunny is mistakenly bitten and starts turning into a vampire. She and Magnus, the vampire she is finding it very difficult to hate, must find a way to make Sunny back into a human. But what they don't count on is finding they have feelings for each other. Will Sunny be able to turn back human? Will she choose humanity over her heart?<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It i light and funny. When I first picked it up I sat down to read the first chapter just to see what it was like and the next thing I knew I was half-way through the book. It's a very easy read and it's so enjoyable you don't really realise how much you are reading.<br />I really liked Sunny. I loved her reaction to finding out about vampires, mainly because she HAD a reaction to it, unlike most female heroines in YA books nowadays. I just thought she was amazing and I totally got why she reacted the way she did to everything that happened to her. She is one of the most likeable main characters and I loved seeing the story from her point of view and seeing it through her eyes. Her personality came across all the way through the book and I loved that. Not every author is able to keep the personlaity of a narrator going through the book all the time but Mari managed to do so effortlessly.<br />Magnus is such an awesome character and I loved him. I love how genuinely sorry he was for Sunny and no matter what he felt all he wanted to do was fix his mistake and make sure Sunny was happy.<br /><br />I love what the author did with her and the irony that was shown throughout the book. The character turned into a vampire is called Sunshine. Yes it's super cheesy but I loved it. I thought it was funny and I kept laughing right the way through the book.<br /><br />I can't wait to see what will happen next and read the next book in the Blood Coven series. I don't know how I will feel about the second book as it is mainly centred on Rainy, Sunny's twin-sister. I wasn't the biggest fan of Rainy, she just irritated me all the way through the book but I will keep reading. I love the style in which this book is wrote. There are definitely not enough light, funny series that centre around such a typically-dark character. Vampire books are typically dark and serious with a very action-packed aspect to the storyline that makes the reader anxious about what will happen. Boys That Bite is not the case at all and I loved that. It's light, funny and the characters have great sense of humours and it's definitely not a book to be taken too seriously and I think that's awesome for a vampire book. I am looking forward to the rest of series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5634630137461355171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer12206769540311161802">Oh my god. <br/><br/>So I picked this book up because it was my favorite book in middle school. I knew it would not be great, and that's exactly what I wanted.<br/>I was prepared for bad writing but nostalgia. Because I read this book in 2006.<br/>What I was not prepared for was this book being reprinted in 2017. <br/>Reprinting isn't a bad thing. Books are reprinted all the time with new covers and new editions.<br/>But never, in my entire life, have I <b>ever</b> read a book that was REWRITTEN. To have the same plot, same charact</span>
  <span id="freeText12206769540311161802" style="display:none">Oh my god. <br /><br />So I picked this book up because it was my favorite book in middle school. I knew it would not be great, and that's exactly what I wanted.<br />I was prepared for bad writing but nostalgia. Because I read this book in 2006.<br />What I was not prepared for was this book being reprinted in 2017. <br />Reprinting isn't a bad thing. Books are reprinted all the time with new covers and new editions.<br />But never, in my entire life, have I <b>ever</b> read a book that was REWRITTEN. To have the same plot, same characters, same everything.... aside from the pop culture references. <br />The author literally wrote her story AGAIN... but she made it relevant to 2017, not 2006. <br /><br />My clearest memory of reading this book the first time was that it introduced Netflix to me. As the DVD subscription service. Bot the streaming service.<br />But this was rewritten so they have a Netflix subscription. The character references Taylor Swift, the Kardashians, Ed Sheeran, and Ian Somerhalder in the Vampire Diaries.<br /><br />I cannot seem to wrap my head around this.<br />That the book was rewritten so it wouldn't be as dated of a book. But in rewriting it so it would be modern, she just left herself open to dating it yet again. In 5 years (I mean, in these two years...) NONE of these names are going to hold any meaning, aside from "oh yeah, they were big a few years ago I guess.)<br /><br />I just.<br />Oh my god.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_959955919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/959955919" />
    <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews"><img alt="Briar&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402183274p2/32054036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/959955919?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fantasy-supernatural">fantasy-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=ya-obsessions">ya-obsessions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=top-books">top-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer959955919&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959955919" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13793201120147780193">Book Title: Boys that Bite (Blood Coven Vampire #1)<br/>Book Author: Mari Mancusi<br/><br/>Introduction: I read this book WAAAAAAAAY back when (like, way back when I was probably in early high school way back) and I absolutely loved it back then. I remember reading this book on the way to a swim meet on a bus filled with athletes who didn't want to talk to me (I was a minor niner who was a great swimmer so I got to go with the grade twelves who were also great swimmers to a meet) so I decided to let my inner b</span>
  <span id="freeText13793201120147780193" style="display:none">Book Title: Boys that Bite (Blood Coven Vampire #1)<br />Book Author: Mari Mancusi<br /><br />Introduction: I read this book WAAAAAAAAY back when (like, way back when I was probably in early high school way back) and I absolutely loved it back then. I remember reading this book on the way to a swim meet on a bus filled with athletes who didn't want to talk to me (I was a minor niner who was a great swimmer so I got to go with the grade twelves who were also great swimmers to a meet) so I decided to let my inner book worm come out. Long story short, I read four books of the series there, and was incredibly upset that I left the rest of the series at home. <br /><br />So, Mari Mancusi rebooted the book from my understanding so of course I wanted to reread it. Out of all the vampire books I obsessed over in my high school years, Mari Mancusi's Blood Coven Vampires was one of my favourite (Alongside Vladimir Todd and Vampire Kisses) so I wanted to get my hands on a copy! And guess what happened? I wiggled my way into a group that reads this very series so I got a copy sent to me!<br /><br />My review is simply a review - it was not requested to be nice, it was simply provide a review and we'll continue throwing this series at you. So how could I argue? I loved this series and I had been meaning to pick it back up as some point anyways! It's my guilty pleasure!<br /><br />Now off to the super spoiler-y review...<br /><br />Review:<br />Rayne and Sunny are adorable. While the names are a tad silly (has anyone actually named their children like this? Please, leave me a link for proof. Maybe I live in too small of a town to see this being common), they are fantastic characters. Re-reading the series makes me wonder why having their names Rayne and Sunny was so important - was it for dramatic effect? Was it to show they are opposites? Was it just for comedy?<br /><br />When Magnus appears, it still makes my heart pound. He was one of my book crushes, and I still adore him. How can you not? He's super hot and a great ying to our Sunny's yang. He's introduced as dark and sexy, which is how you want a YA/teen heart throb to be introduced. Mari does an incredible job expanding on his character -he's not just tall, dark, handsome and brooding. Slowly over the course of this series she delves deeper into this. Now as an adult, I really appreciate that. As a teenie bopper, YA-teenage addict back in the day, I wasn't as appreciative of the hard work she put in.<br /><br />Bonus Marks: Shout out to Emma Stone!!<br /><br />Cheesey factor aside, I really did enjoy the entire Sunny accidentally stepping in for Rayne portion of this novel. It's early on, and you can see it coming if you love your soap operas (like I do...), but it's still a great way to get this series started. It starts the series off with a bang and makes the entire potential plot flip upside down. What do you do if you accidentally step in and become a vampire instead of your sister? It's a great start! I still enjoy it, despite the slight cheesiness that goes along with it.<br /><br />Mari is also the queen of vampire comedy. Random comments fly left and right (sarcastically, insultingly, and many other forms of comedy) and it makes this book better. Does it make it cheesey? Probably. Is this supposed to be a Shakespearean YA novel? Nope!! So it fits in perfectly! This book has a splash of comedy in it! That's one of the great aspects of it!<br /><br />Bonus Marks: "Vamps-R-Us.com" and the Batman reference. Mari knows the way to my heart...<br /><br />Overall, this book still holds up for me. When I was a teenager it was a lot "cooler" - the tone definitely fits a YA audience. Since I'm an adult now, I really do enjoy it. It's funny, slightly cheesey, and has the perfect amounts of romance, drama and comedy to make a really great book. <br /><br />This book won't be for everyone, but as a throwback for me it's excellent. I definitely suggest this book to those who like the YA genre, who want just a splash of cheesey, soap opera-y drama or who want to read a different take on the vampire genre. <br /><br />Forewarning: This book sounds like it's written by a teenager (isn't that kind of the point? The narrators are sixteen years old?). I have seen many, many, many, many complaints about this but you need to understand: THE NARRATORS ARE SIXTEEN YEARS OLD. If you have a problem with that, you need to see that this book is a YA novel. It's not a steamy, EL James Fifty Shades of Grey or Shakespearean novel. It's a YA vampire novel. That is all.<br /><br />Five out of five stars!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13793201120147780193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1967921905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1967921905" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4286573-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390709350p2/4286573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1967921905?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/4286573-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4286573-linda?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4286573-linda?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4286573-linda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4286573-linda?shelf=romance">romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1967921905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17075858776921766980">A cute, light and entertaining YA vampiric romance! <br/><br/>You know, being bitten by a vampire one week before prom really sucks.<br/>	<br/>Boys That Bite by Mari Mancusi is the first cute, light and entertaining installment in the author’s The Blood Coven Vampires series. This is a series that I’ve wanted to delve into ever since I first heard about it described as being attractive to Buffy/Angel fans at the Coastal Magic Convention a year ago. Now that the whole series is being re-released in new updated e-boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17075858776921766980" style="display:none">A cute, light and entertaining YA vampiric romance! <br /><br />You know, being bitten by a vampire one week before prom really sucks.<br />	<br />Boys That Bite by Mari Mancusi is the first cute, light and entertaining installment in the author’s The Blood Coven Vampires series. This is a series that I’ve wanted to delve into ever since I first heard about it described as being attractive to Buffy/Angel fans at the Coastal Magic Convention a year ago. Now that the whole series is being re-released in new updated e-book form, this seemed like the perfect time to jump on board. Now I’m wondering why I waited so long to start it, as I was captivated by it all! <br /><br />As the story opens, we meet sixteen-year-old identical twins, Sunshine “Sunny” and Rayne McDonald. They are five-foot-four with dirty blond hair and brown eyes. However, while they may look similar, they are worlds apart in their natures. Sunny explicitly follows the rules and is an A-student while Rayne … does neither. Sunny has a crush on Jake Wilder at school and is officially on cloud nine as Jake has asked her to go to the prom with him. On the other hand, Rayne is into the Goth scene. She wears nothing but black and even hosts a blog about vampires. <br /><br />On this particular day, Rayne guilt-trips Sunny into accompanying her to a Goth club, Club Fang, that evening. The scene is not to Sunny’s liking, but Sunny is captivated by a hot guy who introduces himself by saying: "Good evening..I'm Magnus..I believe you were expecting me.” In reality, Sunny wasn’t expecting him, nor the bite on the neck he gave her thinking she was her twin sister, Rayne. From that point on, Sunny’s life took a dark turn…<br /><br />I absolutely loved both Sunny and Magnus. Sunny’s essence was genuine wholesome sunshine and her personality and interactions took me back to my high school days. She was easy to relate to. On the other hand, Magnus was the epitome of a tortured hero and swoonworthy. He had been an Arthurian knight and was beyond gallant in his relationship with Sunny. My heart went out to him when it was disclosed how long he’d waited for a blood mate only to be foiled by a mistaken identity crisis. Unfortunately, any romantic relationship between this mis-matched couple seemed doomed from the start. Regardless, I couldn’t help but hold out hope for everyone’s happiness. Boys That Bite is YA-friendly. There’s some kissing, but no hanky panky.<br /><br />Following please find a few of my favorite quotes from Boys That Bite:<br /> <br />	Turning into a vampire is bad enough – I don’t need to flunk out of school on top of it.<br />--- <br />	“You are my blood mate,” he says simply, finding my hand and squeezing it with his own. “I would die for you.”<br />	Gah! A little warning before the touching would be nice. Mainly so I can resist the overwhelming urge to morph into a jiggly pile of Jell-O, thank you very much.<br />	“You’d … die… for me?”” I manage to choke out…. “Technically aren’t you already dead?”<br />--- <br />	Hi, my name is Sunny and I’m a bloodoholic.<br /><br />This is the first book I’ve ever read by Mari Mancusi but it certainly won’t be the last. Mari’s writing is top-notch and the world and the characters she has created are incredible. While this is a vampiric paranormal urban fantasy, Mari’s spin on the concept is unique. This story is laugh-out-loud funny and action-packed. It kept me riveted from the first sentence through to the surprising twist at the end which left me smiling and craving more. Truly, if you are a fan of the Buffy series, you need to check this series out too! I can’t wait to start the next book, Stake That, which will feature Rayne. It appears that Rayne may, in actuality, be a vampire slayer. Oh my!<br /><br />My full review is posted at Reading Between The Wines Book Club. Please check it out there: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingbetweenthewinesbookclub.com/2017/04/4-wine-glass-review-for-boys-that-bite.html">http://www.readingbetweenthewinesbook...</a><br /><br />Suggested Reading Order: <br />The Blood Coven Vampire series:<br />Boys that Bite (Book #1)<br />Stake That (Book #2)<br />Girls that Growl (Book #3)<br />Bad Blood (Book #4)<br />Night School (Book #5)<br />Blood Ties (Book #6)<br />Soul Bound (Book #7)<br />Blood Forever (Book *8)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17075858776921766980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21550232?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-personally-by-moi">read-personally-by-moi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21550232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3740253953381310997">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Sunshine "Sunny" McDonald was doing pretty well; the hottest guy at Oakridge High School, Jake Wilder, has asked her to go to the prom with him, and life is now complete. At five foot four, with dirty blond hair and unimpressive muddy brown eyes, Sunny would have sworn that Jake didn't even know she existed. Freckles notwithstanding, she's not as easily recognizable as her twin sister, Rayne, who's so into the Goth scene, vampires, and wearing all black that it</span>
  <span id="freeText3740253953381310997" style="display:none">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Sunshine "Sunny" McDonald was doing pretty well; the hottest guy at Oakridge High School, Jake Wilder, has asked her to go to the prom with him, and life is now complete. At five foot four, with dirty blond hair and unimpressive muddy brown eyes, Sunny would have sworn that Jake didn't even know she existed. Freckles notwithstanding, she's not as easily recognizable as her twin sister, Rayne, who's so into the Goth scene, vampires, and wearing all black that it's not even funny. Yes, life is looking up--until Sunny lets herself get guilt tripped into attending Club Fang, a cheesy Goth club filled with wannabe vampires, and suddenly her life isn't so sunny anymore. <br /><br />The night starts out okay--yes, the club is the epitome of cheesy and the smoke machine is making her cough--but improves vastly when an Orlando Bloom (Pirates of the Caribbean Orlando, not Lord of the Rings Orlando)introduces himself with a "Good evening..I'm Magnus..I believe you were expecting me" line. Sunny sure wasn't expecting him, and she definitely was not expecting the bite on the neck she gets from the totally hot Magnus. <br /><br />Suddenly life is taking a dark turn, when Sunny finds out that Magnus is not only a vampire--for real!--but that he mistook her for her twin sister, Rayne. Now Sunny's going to turn into one of the undead--this close to prom!--unless she find the Holy Grail. Which is the one and only thing that can reverse the process of turning into a vampire. But even with thoughts of Jake Wilder on the brain, Sunny's not so sure that being a vampire would be so horrible, or that being in league with Magnus would be the end of her life. <br /><br />BOYS THAT BITE is a funny, action-packed read that will keep you turning pages long into the night. The characters--from Sunny, Rayne, Magnus, and everyone in between--are all well-rounded people, and the dialogue is smart and funny. As the three race to save Sunny from an eternal life as a member of the undead, she'll have to find out what's most important in life. And the ending, including a stunner regarding Rayne, definitely sets up the scene for a sequel. A great read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3740253953381310997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477505-mandy?shelf=love-it">love-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477505-mandy?shelf=rd-reviews">rd-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477505-mandy?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477505-mandy?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264805703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4976778428740733743">Sunny’s sister has convinced her to join her at a goth club little did Sunny know that the guy flirting with her really was a vampire. Or that his bite would start the transformation into becoming a vampire was meant for her sister. Not only does Sunny have to worry about becoming a but there is also a vampire slayer out there who could be after her. At least Bertha the slayer has seen better days so she should be able to avoid her.<br/><br/>The only chance to change Sunny back into a human is to drink fr</span>
  <span id="freeText4976778428740733743" style="display:none">Sunny’s sister has convinced her to join her at a goth club little did Sunny know that the guy flirting with her really was a vampire. Or that his bite would start the transformation into becoming a vampire was meant for her sister. Not only does Sunny have to worry about becoming a but there is also a vampire slayer out there who could be after her. At least Bertha the slayer has seen better days so she should be able to avoid her.<br /><br />The only chance to change Sunny back into a human is to drink from the holy grail which happens to be in England. While Sunny may not be on the up when it comes to vampire her twin sister is having a blog all about it. At school at last Sunny has drawn the attention her long time crush he even asks her to prom. Now I only they can find the cup and get back to town before Prom.<br /><br />I like Sunny a lot while more than I do her twin sister, but maybe that’s because her sister doesn’t have a big role in this book. I like that even though Sunny is tossed into the supernatural world she handles it well accepting her fate and dashing off with a strange vampire to stop the transition. I like Magnus when we learned the truth behind how long he’s waited for a blood mate my heart went out to him. I also like the way things worked out for both of them.<br /><br />I’ve had Boys that Bite on my kindle for so long I forgot that it was even on it. I’ve been craving a YA vampire novel so I decided to give it a shot and wasn’t disappointed. While the vampire concept isn’t original the author has added her own unique spin creating a captivating paranormal romance. I really loved the characters I found Sunny easy to connect with after all she’s just like I was back in the day as a teen. This isn’t the first book I’ve read by the author so I knew I would love her writing style which I did. I love all the pop culture references scattered throughout the book. A fast paced action packed whirlwind adventure that I found hard to put down. I enjoyed every moment of Boys that Bite it’s a beautifully written story. I look forward to reading the rest of the series the next one is on my kindle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4976778428740733743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10601251908443586185">When you have no cable or Internet, you must turn water into wine.<br/><br/>I had nothing better to do for the entire month of January so I was like hey, why not catch up on my reading cause I literally hadn't read a book in months since January and that's just not like me. I have a ton of e-books gathering dust and consuming memory space on my computer that I just can't bear to delete because I'm always like: "Yeah, I'll totally read them in my spare time!" I literally spent hours playing spider solitair</span>
  <span id="freeText10601251908443586185" style="display:none">When you have no cable or Internet, you must turn water into wine.<br /><br />I had nothing better to do for the entire month of January so I was like hey, why not catch up on my reading cause I literally hadn't read a book in months since January and that's just not like me. I have a ton of e-books gathering dust and consuming memory space on my computer that I just can't bear to delete because I'm always like: "Yeah, I'll totally read them in my spare time!" I literally spent hours playing spider solitaire instead of reading but finally convinced myself, I needed to regain some brain cells in time for school and decided to read one of aforementioned e-books and I chose this one.<br /><br />I'm going to keep this short and sweet.<br /><br />I didn't pay for this book (someone sent it to me) and you shouldn't either.<br /><br />It was slightly funny but very cliche and predictable. You read this when you're constipated and need to pass time in the bathroom. At least that's why I think people read on the toilet....<br /><br />ANYWAYS, It was just too out there and a bit childish and I know this review sounds harsh but this was just not worth my time. I will not be reading the rest of the series. <br /><br />Sunny was rude, the stereotypes and the jokes made about stereotypes and Magnus falling in love with Sunny and the trip to England and her hippie mother and their names (Sunny and Rayne. How many different languages can I express my intense hatred for authors who try to be cute by coming up with unusual names. If it's not a dystopian or relevant to the story or not cheesy or vomit-inducing, go ahead, make up your own name or use something unique. Otherwise....please just sit down and stop.), the whole Vampire Council crap.....I just can't.<br /><br />NO. <br /><br />If you like light, cheesy yet just a tad funny, books then you have found your cup of tea.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5124059372436055014">You know when you think "I'm not sure where to start" well that's what I feeling right now, <br/><br/>Okay first things first, Sunshine and Rayne are twin sisters. And Rayne is going to go to a club to be turned into a vampire and live happily ever after with Magnus. Well, personally, if I was going to a club to be turned into a vampire, I wouldn't bring my twin sister along. I mean what was she thinking.<br/>"Oh yeah, I'm just going to invite my sister to the club where I'm going to be turned into a vampire" </span>
  <span id="freeText5124059372436055014" style="display:none">You know when you think "I'm not sure where to start" well that's what I feeling right now, <br /><br />Okay first things first, Sunshine and Rayne are twin sisters. And Rayne is going to go to a club to be turned into a vampire and live happily ever after with Magnus. Well, personally, if I was going to a club to be turned into a vampire, I wouldn't bring my twin sister along. I mean what was she thinking.<br />"Oh yeah, I'm just going to invite my sister to the club where I'm going to be turned into a vampire" yeah, real smart thinking. <br />And what's with all the celebrity look a likes? I mean seriously, she couldn't go without a page writing about how someone looks like this or someone likes that that. <br />And what's up with Bertha? She's described as fat, pimpled face, and has braces. And so in like two lines she kills the vampire leader? You know for a vampire who has more strength and has lived longer then a fat pimpled face girl, I thought he would at least do something rather than stand there. Jeez....<br />Oh and don't get me started on the Holy Grail. It was SO easy for Magnus and Sunshine to find! They got to this town, dance and party, kiss and then go to this little house and Magnus offers money and the dude goes, "yep let me just talk about that with someone". Then he comes back and simply shows them the holy grail. He just leads them down some creepy hallways, and a staircase and boom, there's the holy grail. WHAT THE HECK?!?! I hated this book and seriously, I don't want to continue the series.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150129632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17276806496834216438">I enjoyed this book all the way through until the end. Then I was disappointed. I liked Sunny and couldn't stand her sister Rayne. Rayne seemed unsympathetic about the plight Sunny found herself in. I guess it would be hard to feel sorry for Sunny when Sunny had what Rayne wanted more than anything. But she had to feel her sister's panic and pain. Rayne was more interested in how bad the vampire was feeling. Some parts were absurd like the overweight vampire slayer. I get that it was to be radic</span>
  <span id="freeText17276806496834216438" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book all the way through until the end. Then I was disappointed. I liked Sunny and couldn't stand her sister Rayne. Rayne seemed unsympathetic about the plight Sunny found herself in. I guess it would be hard to feel sorry for Sunny when Sunny had what Rayne wanted more than anything. But she had to feel her sister's panic and pain. Rayne was more interested in how bad the vampire was feeling. Some parts were absurd like the overweight vampire slayer. I get that it was to be radically different from Buffy or something, but wow, overweight? No way an overweight human is going to kill a vampire unless she gets the drop on him while he's sleeping. It's just silly.<br /><br />Another crazy inclusion was that all of this vampire information was supposed to be kept secret from the world, but the vampires had encouraged Rayne to keep a blog about every single detail of her journey to becoming a vampire. What? How could the author and editors miss that little detail? Don't they know a blog is public?<br /><br />I will probably read the rest of the series, but because I abhorred the ending of this book and because I never did start liking Rayne, it will be a bit while I read the rest of the books I've purchased. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17276806496834216438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
